FAIR OAKS RECREATION AND PARK DISTRICT BOARD OF
                                   DIRECTORS
ONE THOUSAND FOUR HUNDRED FORTY-FIRST BOARD OF DIRECTORS’
                    REGULAR MEETING
               Agenda for February 19, 2025
The regular meeting of the Board of Directors on February 19, 2025 will be conducted in
                                 person and via Zoom:
                       https://us02web.zoom.us/j/87345380207
                                  US: +1 669 900 9128
                               Meeting ID: 873 453 80207


                          FAIR OAKS WATER DISTRICT

                               February 19, 2025
                                   6:00 P.M.
1. CALL TO ORDER

2. PLEDGE OF ALLEGIANCE

3. ROLL CALL

4. PRESENTATIONS/PROCLAMATIONS/RECOGNITION

  4.I. Parkway Disc Golf Foundation Presentation.

5. AUDIENCE/PUBLIC COMMENT (NON-AGENDA ITEMS)
    (Any person may address the Board upon any subject within the jurisdiction
    of the Fair Oaks Recreation and Park Distict. Each speaker is limited to a
    maximum of THREE (3) minutes. Any matter requiring Board action will be
    referred to staff or committee for a report and action at a subsequent
    meeting).

6. CONSENT CALENDAR
    (All matters listed under Consent Calendar are considered by the Board of Directors to
    be routine and will be acted upon in a single motion. There will not be separate
    discussions of these items unless a request is made prior to the time the Board
    considers a motion to approve).

 Note: Regarding Sick-Leave hours, a Regular Full-Time employee may choose the Sick Leave payout option and utilize a maximum of
   320 hours (as identified within the table above) which will be compensated at 50% of the employees current hourly rate of pay.
However, upon retirement from the District, a Regular Full-Time employee December choose to utilize their accrued Sick Leave toward
CalPERS service credit with no maximum limit. Employees whose Sick Leave hours exceed 320 hours are noted but the hours in excess
of 320 not calculated as a liability in the table above. A Regular Part-Time employee will be compensated for a maximum of 160 hours
                                    of sick leave at 50% of the employees rate of pay upon termination.

Extension Narrative for Construction Project 2/19/25

Site Adjustments:

   •   Ongoing grade revisions have been necessary at the playground to address installation
       and drainage requirements.
   •   Additional concrete work and re-work have been incorporated to meet changing
       specifications and ensure long-term durability.
   •   Completion activities such as site planting and installation of site furnishings are pending,
       which are critical to the final appearance and functionality of the park areas.

Community Center (CC):

   •   Modifications to the exterior seating by the owner prompted a delay in adjacent concrete
       work to prevent damage to newly installed materials.
   •   Changes to stage doors and ADA modifications to the entry ramp have been implemented
       to enhance accessibility and functionality.
   •   Interior finishes, including flooring, are on hold until external construction activities are
       completed to avoid damage.

Clubhouse (CH):

   •   Changes in permitting requirements and adjustments to the kitchen design have led to
       delays.
   •   Window specifications were modified by the owner, necessitating a reevaluation of
       installation timelines.
   •   Similar to the Community Center, finishing works like flooring are delayed to protect
       them during the ongoing external construction.

General Delays:

   •   Adverse weather conditions have repeatedly caused delays, particularly affecting outdoor
       work like paving, which requires specific weather conditions for tasks such as laying
       asphalt.
   •   The irregular start/stop nature of work has caused scheduling conflicts with
       subcontractors, requiring significant effort to reschedule once work scopes are clarified
       and conditions improve.

                 FAIR OAKS RECREATION AND PARK DISTRICT
        ONE THOUSAND FOUR HUNDRED AND FORTIETH BOARD OF DIRECTORS’
                             REGULAR MEETING

                               Minutes for January 15, 2025

The one thousand four hundred and fortieth meeting of the Fair Oaks Recreation and Park District
Board of Directors was held on Wednesday, January 15, 2025, at the Fair Oaks Water District, 10326
Fair Oaks Blvd., Fair Oaks, CA.

For the Record:                     Chair Tamagni called the regular meeting to order at 6:00 PM.

Board Members Present:              Chair Tamagni, Director Carhart, Director Irwin, Director
                                    Mounts

Board Members Absent:               Vice-Chair O’Farrell

Staff Present:                      District Administrator Mike Aho, Administrative Assistant II
                                    Ian Roberts, Administrative Services Manager Jennifer
                                    Larkin, Arts and Entertainment Manager Jennifer Schuler,
                                    Parks and Facilities Manager Sean Ventura, Recreation
                                    Manager Nick Davison, Recreation Supervisor Mary Stoakley

Members of the Public:              7

PRESENTATIONS:
Recreation Manager Nick Davison presented the Year in Review.

PUBLIC COMMENT:
Leon Corcos of Fair Oaks spoke to the Board regarding the playground in Village Park, the re-
paving of the streets around the park and parking meter support.

Lindsay Kopperud of Fair Oaks spoke to the Board in appreciation of the changes that have been
made at the Miller Park disc golf course.

Rebecca Christianson of Fair Oaks spoke to the Board in appreciation of the changes that have
been made at the Miller Park disc golf course.

DISCUSSION & ACTION #1:            Consent Calendar
A motion to approve the consent calendar was made by Director Irwin and seconded by Director
Mounts.
AYES:         Chair Tamagni, Director Carhart, Director Irwin, Director Mounts
NOES:         None
ABSTAIN:      None
ABSENT:       Vice-Chair O’Farrell
RECUSE:       None

DISCUSSION & ACTION #2:
Monthly Fair Oaks Youth Advisory Report.
Matthew Cao, FOYAB Chair, gave the January report.

Timothy Mattheis
           STAFF REPORT


Meeting Date:        January 15, 2025

To:                  Board of Directors

From:                Michael J. Aho – District Administrator

Subject:             Approval of a Change Order of $77,454.71 for
                     Veteran Memorial Amphitheatre Hanger Doors

I.     Recommendation
       Authorize the District Administrator to sign the Change Order (Attachment
       A) for the Amphitheater Hangar Door in the amount of $77,454.17.

II.    Background
       The Veterans Memorial Amphitheater, part of our Measure J project, is
       equipped with a substantial hangar door that fronts the stage. This door is
       integral to the facility's security, allowing it to be secured when not in use.
       Additionally, its design supports the dual use of the space, including the
       Black Box Theater, making it a versatile, year-round performance facility.
       The door plays a critical role in temperature control within the venue, aiding
       in both heating and cooling, thus ensuring a comfortable environment for
       performances and events throughout the year.

III.   Problem /Situation/ Request
       During the installation process, unforeseen structural challenges and
       changes in material availability necessitated modifications to the original
       door design. Specifically, the original 2-inch-thick panels intended for the
       door have been discontinued, requiring a shift to 1.5-inch-thick panels. This
       change means that the eight panels needed for the two doors now require
       new framing, flashing, support brackets, and weather stripping to
       accommodate the different panel thickness. These modifications have led
       to an increase in costs. The attached detailed Change Order accounts for
       these necessary adjustments and associated costs, which exceed the
       $70,000 threshold and therefore require Board approval.
IV.    Financial Analysis
       The total additional cost for this Change Order is $77,454.17. This expense,
       along with two other Change Orders related to the seating replacement —
       one for $102,200 for seating demolition and material removal, and another
       for $121,996 for electrical work and trenching — will be covered by the
       existing contract allowance with Bobo Construction. These expenses will
       deplete the existing $1,800,000 contingency allowance included in our
       construction contract with Bobo Construction. However, the contract with
       Bobo will be increased by $667,335 to fund the seating renovation, as
       approved by the Board. Once this increase is finalized, we will be able to
       credit the allowance of $224,196 for the seating costs.
        Furthermore, the staff anticipates additional changes to the Bobo
       Construction Contract and Allowance due to upcoming road work around
       the park. These upcoming modifications will be funded by the $1,400,000
       Senate Appropriation funds awarded through Senator Padilla's office. More
       details on these changes will be presented to the Board as they become
       available.



Respectfully Submitted,



Michael J. Aho
District Administrator

Attachment A: Change Order
Attachment A
           STAFF REPORT

Meeting Date:        February 19, 2025

To:                  Board of Directors

From:                Mike Aho – District Administrator

Subject:             Future Location of Fair Oaks Chicken Festival

Prepared By:         Sabrina Bernardo – Recreation Supervisor

I.     Recommendation
Approve Fair Oaks Park as the location for the annual Fair Oaks Chicken Festival,
with staff exploring a prelude or extended event in the Village of Fair Oaks, as
supported by the Community Resources Development Committee and District staff.

II.    Background
In 2008, the District became the organizer and presenter of the Fair Oaks Chicken
Festival, which was held in the Village of Fair Oaks through 2019. The festival was
canceled in 2020 due to COVID-19 but returned in 2021. Due to construction in
the Village, the festival was relocated to Fair Oaks Park, where it most recently
celebrated its 19th annual event in September 2024.

III.   Problem /Situation/ Request

With construction in the Village estimated to be complete in late Spring 2025, a
decision must be made regarding whether the Fair Oaks Chicken Festival will
return to the Village of Fair Oaks or remain at its current location in Fair Oaks
Park. Staff conducted a thorough evaluation of both locations to determine the
festival's future venue. Based on this assessment, Fair Oaks Park is
recommended as the location due to its logistical advantages, enhanced safety
features, and greater capacity for future growth.

   •   Venue Analysis Summary (see attachment A Venue Analysis)
Parking & Road Closures:
Fair Oaks Park provides approximately 360 usable parking spaces
managed by the Fair Oaks Recreation & Park District (FORPD), with
additional parking, approximately 340 spaces, available at Fair Oaks
Church through the Districts Joint Use Agreement. Controlled parking
allows for dedicated ADA-compliant spaces and paid options. The lack of
required road closures helps minimize staffing needs and costs.

In contrast, the Village has limited confirmed parking, and any additional
spaces that may be available could require special permissions or fees,
potentially still falling short of accommodating the estimated attendance.
Neighbors and merchants will face significant access challenges. Road
closures on Fair Oaks Blvd., California, and Park Streets necessitate
permits, barricades, and additional staffing, adding to both costs and
logistical complexity.


Space, Layout & Logistics: Fair Oaks Park offers expansive open
spaces, shade trees, and grassy areas, creating a comfortable and secure
environment for attendees. Its layout facilitates easy setup, event
expansion, controlled access, and advanced inspections. The District,
partners, and vendors have the ability to set up in advance, reducing
stress on the day of the event. Additionally, the park's proximity to the
maintenance yard simplifies equipment transportation, and event setup
and park closures are more manageable and secure.


In contrast, the Village has limited space and narrow roads, causing
congestion and restricting room for attractions. Road closures add
logistical complexity and ensuring a safe and enjoyable festival would
require full cooperation from local businesses and neighbors, complicating
planning further.

Festivities: Fair Oaks Park accommodates an expanded food court, two
beer and wine concession areas, a larger Kids Park with free and paid
zones, cornhole tournament, and additional vendor opportunities,
including Activity Booths and Kid's Big Business booths. The park’s layout
supports these enhancements, enriching the event experience and
attracting a broader audience. In contrast, the Village’s space constraints
would require significant downsizing or elimination of activities, limiting
the festival's appeal.

Safety: The park offers a controlled environment with fencing and
designated entry and exit points, enhancing safety for attendees, staff,
and volunteers. In contrast, the Village lacks such controls, allowing
unrestricted entry and exit, which prevents effective safety checks and
increases risks associated with alcohol, unauthorized substances, and
weapons being brought into the event area. Emergency situations, such
          as locating a lost child, become more difficult to manage without
          monitored gates. Additionally, crowded streets and unauthorized business
          extensions into the event layout compromise the designated 20-foot fire
          lane, posing challenges for emergency response. The proximity to
          vehicular traffic and the need to staff numerous barricades further
          increase risks to staff, volunteers, and attendees.

          ADA: Staff believe Fair Oaks Park is the better choice for managing and
          mitigating ADA access to the festival. The park’s ample, clearly marked
          ADA parking near the main entrance makes arrival and access more
          convenient for attendees with mobility needs. Additionally, FORPD-owned
          ADA trekking can be laid in advance, ensuring accessibility without
          requiring additional rentals or staff coordination on the day of the event.
          The Village, despite recent renovations improving accessibility, faces
          significant ADA parking limitations for an event of this size, making access
          to the festival more difficult and requiring staff and volunteers to
          coordinate access on the day of the event.

          Staffing: Fair Oaks Park requires fewer staff and fewer overall staff hours
          while providing a smoother experience for both staff, vendors, partners,
          and attendees. Staff report fewer issues and enjoy working at the event,
          with easy on-site parking at the maintenance shop. In contrast, hosting
          the event in the Village presents significant challenges to staff, including
          logistical difficulties with staff parking, increased complaints from the
          public about road closures and access, and safety concerns due to
          frustrated drivers disregarding barricades.

      •   Partner and Vendor Survey Summary (see Attachment B –
          Partner and Vendor Survey): The majority of vendors and partner
          groups prefer Fair Oaks Park due to its ample space, accessibility, and
          logistical advantages. Nearly all respondents indicated they would
          continue participating if the festival remains at this location. However, if
          the event were moved to the Village, some respondents shifted from "very
          likely" to "likely" to participate, while others indicated they would be "not
          likely" or "unlikely" to return.

          While the downtown Village offers unique charm and strong community
          support, most partners and vendors find that challenges related to
          parking, space, and logistics outweigh the benefits.

      •   Staff Survey Summary (see attachment C Staff Survey):
          Overwhelming preference to keep Chicken Festival at Fair Oaks Park due
          to better space, parking, safety, and overall event experience. While some
          miss the village ambiance, the logistical and space challenges of holding
          Chicken Festival in the Village make it less desirable.

IV.       Financial Analysis
Staff believes that hosting the event at Fair Oaks Park is far more cost-effective
than returning to the Village. Hosting in the Village would require additional
staffing hours, higher rental costs, and potential fees for CHP traffic control due to
road closures. Additional expenses could include securing parking lots to ensure
ADA accessibility and attendees parking and/or hiring shuttle services to transport
attendees to and from remote parking areas.

The Village's limited space and lack of FORPD controlled parking would further
restrict or eliminate activities such as the paid Kids' Park, cornhole tournaments,
vendor booths, food trucks, alcohol sales and paid parking, significantly reducing
key revenue streams. With increased costs and substantial revenue losses, hosting
the event in the Village would result in operating at a deficit.

V.      Conclusion
While the Village of Fair Oaks offers a unique and historic setting, its limitations
in space, parking, safety, and logistics make it less suitable for large-scale events
like the Chicken Festival. In contrast, Fair Oaks Park provides ample space,
controlled parking, enhanced safety measures, and a layout that supports a
broader range of attractions and future event growth. The park’s established
infrastructure and adaptability ensures a safer, more enjoyable, and seamless
experience for attendees, staff, and vendors. Additionally, hosting the festival at
Fair Oaks Park is more financially viable, avoiding increased staffing and
equipment costs, logistical challenges, and lost revenue associated with returning
to the Village. For these reasons, Fair Oaks Park is the best choice for the long-
term success of the festival.

Staff appreciates the Board's support and respectfully requests a timely decision
on the location of the 2025 Fair Oaks Chicken Festival to allow adequate time for
planning and preparation.

Respectfully Submitted,


Michale Aho
District Administrator

Attachment A- Venue Analysis
Attachment B- Partner & Vendor Survey
Attachment C- Staff Survey
 ATTACHMENT A - VENUE ANALYSIS

           Fair Oaks Chicken Festival: Venue Analysis

Parking & Road Closures

Fair Oaks Park:
    • Advantages:
          o Approximately 360 usable FORPD owned and operated parking spaces. An
             additional 340 spaces are available at Fair Oaks Church through our Joint
             Use Agreement.
          o Controlled parking lots facilitate ADA and paid parking.
          o No road closures needed, reducing staff and equipment costs.
    • Challenges:
          o Some attendees park in unauthorized and nonmarketed parking areas,
             potentially inconveniencing local businesses or residents.
Village:
    • Advantages:
          o None noted.
    • Challenges:
          o Approximately 12 usable FORPD owned and operated parking spaces in the
             District Office lot, though these are used for district vehicles and sponsor
             parking. Additional parking may be available at the ATT lot, Edward Jones,
             Meraki, Scandinavian Designs, Tudors, the Water District, along Bridge
             Street, and surrounding neighborhoods. However, access to these lots is
             uncertain and may require fees, staffing, permits, or special permissions.
          o Uncontrolled FORPD parking hinders ADA parking compliance.
          o Narrow roads and limited parking options create challenges for attendees
             and staff.
          o Roads (Fair Oaks Blvd., California, Park) require closures, permits, signage,
             barricades, and staffing, thus increasing staff time and equipment expenses.
          o A request will need to be submitted to re-route SacRT buses.
          o Road closures displace merchants and neighbors, create access issues, and
             increase staffing needs.
          o Road closure and limited parking options may hurt or cause appointment
             based businesses to close day of the event.
          o To minimize the impact on Village businesses and parking availability, while
             ensuring no vehicles are left overnight or parked within the event area, staff
             or contracted services monitor and close portions of parking as businesses
             close, often as late as 1 a.m.
          o To keep the event area vehicle-free, road closures begin at 3:30 a.m.,
             requiring additional staff time and expenses.
          o Road closures around the Village cause detours and driver frustrations.
          o  Due to road closures and limited parking availability staff must park at Fair
             Oaks Park and be shuttled back and forth to the village, causing extra
             coordination and time.
   •   Advantages:
          o None noted.


Space, Layout, and Logistics

Fair Oaks Park:
    • Advantages:
          o Provides open grass spaces, shade trees, and a secure fenced area with
             lockable gates.
          o Setup can be completed in advance without disrupting businesses or
             causing accessibility issues. This approach allows most of the setup to occur
             during regular work hours, reducing staff time and minimizing long hours.
          o Expansive layout allows for growth and improved event features.
          o Proximity to the maintenance yard simplifies equipment transport.
          o With the majority of the setup completed and vendor spaces marked in
             advance, the Fire Inspection can typically be conducted on the Friday before
             the event. This eliminates the overtime inspection fee and allows staff to
             focus on event day operations.
    • Challenges:
          o Limited downtown appeal.
Village:
    • Advantages:
          o Known as the heart of Fair Oaks with a unique, eclectic vibe and proximity to
             local businesses.
          o Potential use of the amphitheater or indoor community rooms for attractions.
          o Downtown location might attract more foot traffic to local Village merchants,
             specifically bars, restaurants, and shops.
    • Challenges:
          o Asphalt surfaces make the area uncomfortably hot.
          o With numerous stakeholders (merchants) in the Village and their varying
             needs, it is challenging to coordinate and satisfy everyone while still adhering
             to Department of Transportation requirements, Fire Code, and ensuring the
             safety of staff and attendees.
          o Limited setup time and lack of security (fencing and park gates) for advanced
             setups.
          o Equipment must be transported from Fair Oaks Park, increasing logistical
             complexity.
          o Recent construction has reduced usable space.
Festivities

Food Court
Fair Oaks Park:
    • Advantages:
          o Space for a larger number of food trucks, allowing for shorter lines and less
             congestion.
          o The park features built-in seating in picnic areas, picnic benches throughout,
             and ample space to accommodate additional tables and chairs provided by
             Sacramento Mobile Food Trucks.
          o If food trucks are eliminated or reduced, the District will lose a valuable
             source of funding (commission) that helps prevent the event from operating
             at a loss.
Challenges:
          o Does not provide direct access to walkable local restaurants.
Village:
    • Advantages:
          o Proximity to walkable local restaurants gives attendees dining options.
          o Likely increase in Village restaurant revenue day of event.
    • Challenges:
          o Recent construction removed the original food court area, necessitating
             either its relocation within the event footprint—reducing space for other
             attractions—or the elimination of food trucks altogether.
          o Lacks seating.

Beer & Wine
Fair Oaks Park:
    • Advantages:
          o Two beer and wine concession areas (one larger, one quick service) due to
             ample space.
          o The controlled, fully fenced environment allows attendees to enjoy
             beverages while walking throughout the entire event.
          o No competition from outside businesses selling beer and wine.
    • Challenges:
          o None noted.
Village:
    • Advantages:
          o None noted.
    • Challenges:
          o The previous beer and wine area in the Village was small and may now
             require fencing for ABC compliance, which could further reduce sales for
             Rotary.
           o   An increase in local restaurants and bars selling alcohol creates
               competition, potentially decreasing sales for Rotary.
           o   Enforcing alcohol restrictions is challenging when multiple entities, such as
               restaurants and bars, are selling alcohol and may or may not abide by the
               events ABC requirements.
           o   Without fencing and designated entry and exit points in the Village, alcohol
               can be freely brought in and out, posing a significant risk to public safety and
               increasing District liability.

Kids Park
Fair Oaks Park:
    • Advantages:
          o Expansive space allows for free and paid kids’ zones with multiple
             attractions.
          o Revenue generated from a paid kid’s zone help to keep the event from
             operating at a loss.
          o Dedicated space for community partner booths, a petting zoo, and
             entrepreneurial opportunities for kids.
          o Located in softball fields for enhanced safety.
    • Challenges
          o None noted.
Village:
    • Advantages:
          o None noted.
    • Challenges:
          o Limited space compared to Fair Oaks Park would significantly reduce or
             eliminate free and paid offerings and would increase wait times for the
             attractions that remain.
          o The traditional location of the Kid’s Park in the Village requires fencing for
             safety, as it is situated along a road that remains open to vehicular traffic.

Vendors
Fair Oaks Park:
   • Advantages:
          o The park space allows for more vendors, increasing revenue, while also
             accommodating Activity Booths and Kid’s Big Business booths to enhance
             the event's offerings.
          o Vendors can preview and/or set up their booths on Friday, reducing the
             number of vendors needing access on the day of the event and relieving
             stress for both vendors and staff.
          o Less staff and coordination are required to check in vendors.
          o Vendor spaces can be safely marked in advance.
   • Challenges:
          o Some vendor spaces are on grass, which may not be ADA accessible for all.
Village:
    • Advantages:
         o None noted.
    • Challenges:
         o Staff must use semi-permanent marking chalk or paint on the asphalt to
            ensure vendors set up correctly and comply with the Fire Code. Due to staff
            limitations and time constraints, spaces must be marked days in advance,
            eliminating the use of chalk.
         o Vendors must navigate road closures and enter their designated gate for
            setup. Failing to do so creates safety hazards, roadblocks, and vendor
            frustrations.
         o Challenges with locating parking.

Cornhole
Fair Oaks Park:
    • Advantages:
          o Large, flat surface in the MP Field allows for cornhole tournaments and
             fundraising opportunities.
    • Challenges:
          o None noted.
Village:
    • Advantages:
          o None noted.
    • Challenges:
          o Limited space would require discontinuing cornhole or eliminating or
             reducing other festivities at the event to make room for the tournament.

Main Stage & Cluck n’ Crow
  • Fair Oaks Park and Village: Both locations are suitable for hosting the main stage
      and Cluck n’ Crow contest and provide similar experiences.

Pancake Breakfast
   • Fair Oaks Park and Village: The Orangevale Fair Oaks Grange prefers to keep
     breakfast at their hall. If the Grange chooses to host on site, both Fair Oaks Park and
     the Village have suitable indoor facilities.

Safety

Fair Oaks Park:
   • Advantages:
          o The park is fenced and fencing does not intrude upon businesses.
          o Fencing and entry/exit gates contribute to a controlled and monitored event
            area helping to reduce likelihood of lost children, unauthorized vendors and
            or vehicle entry.
         o Entry/exit gates create a secure environment and allows for bag checks that
            search for alcohol, unauthorized substances, and weapons.
         o The park provides ample space to accommodate attractions while meeting
            Sac Metro Fire requirements, including maintaining 20 feet of clearance
            between tents/canopies and buildings or vehicles, 20-foot fire lanes on
            roads, 12 feet between groupings of tents/canopies exceeding 700 square
            feet, and ensuring generators are fenced and located at least 20 feet from
            tents/canopies.
         o Since moving to Fair Oaks Park, staff have noted a significant decrease of
            lost children, believed to be attributed to the enclosed layout and increased
            safety procedures,
    • Challenges:
         o None noted.
Village:
    • Advantages:
         o None noted.
    • Challenges:
         o An open event without controlled and monitored gates for safety checks
            increases the risk of unauthorized items being brought into the event area.
         o Alcohol cannot be effectively monitored without gated entry and exit points,
            allowing it to be brought in and out freely.
         o Asphalt surfaces are hotter and less comfortable for attendees.
         o Compliance with fire code regulations requires cooperation from
            stakeholders/business owners.
         o Road closures around the Village cause detours and driver frustrations
            putting staff and volunteers at risk of injury or harassment from drivers.

ADA Accessibility

Fair Oaks Park:
    • Advantages:
          o Ample ADA parking close to the main entrance.
          o Clearly marked ADA parking area for easy access upon arrival.
          o Staff can proactively address accessibility challenges by laying ADA trekking
             days in advance (owned by FORPD), freeing up resources during the event.
    • Challenges:
          o Grass surfaces require ADA trekking to be laid for accessibility.
Village:
    • Advantages:
          o Improved ADA accessibility with recent renovations.
   •   Challenges:
         o Insufficient ADA-designated parking; available spaces are sporadic, not
             FORPD-owned, and may require fees, staffing, or special permissions for
             use. Additional staff or volunteers will likely be needed to manage these
             spaces.
         o With ADA parking scattered throughout the Village and road closures in
             place, navigation would be more difficult for attendees with mobility needs.

Staffing

                       Staffing Snippet: Village vs. Fair Oaks Park
                               2018-         2019- 2023- Fair Oaks       2024 - Fair Oaks
                             Village       Village               Park                Park
 Number of Staff                  31            31                 24                  25
 Total Day of Hours
 Worked                        437.5           410              279.5                 303
                              5-17.5      8.5-16.5
 Shift Range                   hours         hours       7.5-15 hours          4-15 hours
 Average Length of                           13.22
 Shift for staff           14 hours          hours        11.64 hours         12.12 hours

Fair Oaks Park:
    • Advantages:
          o Fewer staff and hours are required to organize the event at Fair Oaks Park.
          o Staff encounter fewer issues and generally enjoy working at the event.
          o Staff can park at the maintenance shop within Fair Oaks Park with no
             problem.
    • Challenges:
          o None noted.
Village:
    • Advantages:
          o None noted.
    • Challenges:
          o Staff must park their personal vehicles at Fair Oaks Park and be shuttled to
             and from the event in District vehicles, creating logistical challenges and
             reducing staff availability during the event due to transportation time.
          o Staff face increased complaints and frustration from individuals due to road
             closures, limited access to appointments and businesses in the Village, ADA
             concerns, and difficulty finding parking.
          o Many staff members have been put in harm's way as drivers, frustrated by the
             closures, speed past or go around barricades and checkpoints, believing
             they should have access.
ATTACHMENT B - PARTNET & VENODR SURVEY
 Dear PartnerNendor,
 Thank you for your participation in the 2024 Fair Oaks Chicken Festival! As you may know,
 the festival was traditionally held in the downtown Village of Fair Oaks but was relocated to
 Fair Oaks Park for the 2021-2024 events due to construction.
While Fair Oaks Park has offered several advantages and contributed to the festival's
success in recent years, we are now considering the possibility of returning to the downtown
Village or permanently keeping the event at Fair Oaks Park.
As a valued partner/vendor, your feedback is important. We would greatly appreciate it if you
could share your thoughts by completing the survey below. Please note that this survey is for
our partner groups/vendors only and only one survey should be completed per partner
group/vendor. Only feedback from an approved 2024 partner/vendor will be reviewed in this
specific survey/feedback form.
Please provide your feedback by November 7, 2024. Please also note that no decisions
have been made-we are currently gathering feedback only. At this stage, we do not have a
definitive date for when the Fair Oaks Recreation & Park District (FORPD) will make the final
decision or who will be involved in that process. We may follow up with partners/vendors
individually for more specific feedback.
Thank you again for your continued support of the Fair Oaks Chicken Festival. We truly value
your input and look forward to hearing your thoughts.


Respondent

You will receive a confirmation by email.

 Dear Partner/Vendor,

Thank you for your participation in the 2024 Fair Oaks Chicken Festival! As you may know,
the festival was traditionally held in the downtown Village of Fair Oaks but was relocated to
Fair Oaks Park for the 2021-2024 events due to construction.

While Fair Oaks Park has offered several advantages and contributed to the festival's
success in recent years, we are now considering the possibility of returning to the downtown
Village or permanently keeping the event at Fair Oaks Park.

As a valued partner/vendor, your feedback is important. We would greatly appreciate it if you
could share your thoughts by completing the survey below. Please note that this survey is for
our partner groups/vendors only and only one survey should be completed per partner
group/vendor. Only feedback from an approved 2024 partner/vendor will be reviewed in this
specific survey/feedback form.

Please provide your feedback by November 7, 2024. Please also note that no decisions
have been made-we are currently gathering feedback only. At this stage, we do not have a
definitive date for when the Fair Oaks Recreation & Park District (FORPD) will make the final
decision or who will be involved in that process. We may follow up with partners/vendors
individually for more specific feedback.

Thank you again for your continued support of the Fair Oaks Chicken Festival. We truly value
your input and look forward to hearing your thoughts.

 the festival was traditionally held in the downtown Village of Fair Oaks but was relocated to
 Fair Oaks Park for the 2021-2024 events due to construction.

 While Fair Oaks Park has offered several advantages and contributed to the festival's
 success in recent years, we are now considering the possibility of returning to the downtown
 Village or permanently keeping the event at Fair Oaks Park.

As a valued partner/vendor, your feedback is important. We would greatly appreciate it if you
could share your thoughts by completing the survey below. Please note that this survey is for
our partner groups/vendors only and only one survey should be completed per partner
group/vendor. Only feedback from an approved 2024 partner/vendor will be reviewed in this
specific survey/feedback form.

Please provide your feedback by November 7, 2024. Please also note that no decisions
have been made-we are currently gathering feedback only. At this stage, we do not have a
definitive date for when the Fair Oaks Recreation & Park District (FORPD) will make the final
decision or who will be involved in that process. We may follow up with partners/vendors
individually for more specific feedback.

Thank you again for your continued support of the Fair Oaks Chicken Festival. We truly value
your input and look forward to hearing your thoughts.



Respondent

You will receive a confirmation by email.

What are the pros of hosting the festival at Fair Oaks Park?

 As someone who has planned events in the village, I believe holding the festival at the
 park is a clear choice. It allows for better crowd control and eliminates concerns about
 street closures and barricades, which can pose safety risks if the event is held in the
 village. The park offers a larger space to accommodate a variety of activities, ensuring a
 more enjoyable experience for everyone. Additionally, there is ample parking for visitors
 and plenty of shade for guests to relax in. Vendors will also appreciate the convenient
 access for loading in and out.
What are the cons of hosting the festival at Fair Oaks Park?

  I'm honestly at a loss for ideas.



How likely are you to continue participating in the festival if it was to remain at Fair
Oaks Park?

@ Very likely
0 Likely
0 Not likely
0 Unlikely


If the event remains at Fair Oaks Park, do you think a smaller kick-off event in the
downtown Village could be successful? Do you have any suggestions for what the
kick-off event could include?

  In my opinion, holding a kickoff event in the village may not be a worthwhile investment of
  time and energy. The success of such an event really hinges on the support of the local
  merchants. Without their backing, organizing a smaller-scale kick-off may not be justified.
  This is just my personal perspective, especially considering the significant effort that goes
  into planning this kind of event.



Have you participated in the festival when it was held in the downtown Village?

@ves
ONo


What were or would you consider as the pros of the downtown Village location?

[jhe atmosphere of the old village transports you to another era



What were or would you consider as the cons/challenges of the downtown Village
location?

 The event has less parking available, and many village merchants are not participating or
 welcoming visitors to shop. Furthermore, the logistics of closing streets and managing
 barricades seem to require even more volunteers and cost. Additionally, the crowd control
 is challenging. In my opinion, it may actually be more costly to close the streets and
 involve law enforcement like CHP or the Sheriff. There is also a noticeable lack of shade,
 seating, and activities for attendees to enjoy.
How would moving the event back to the Village impact your participation and sales as
a partner group/vendor?

  Since we are now hosting the cornhole tournament, I don't believe we have enough space
  to organize an additional activity. Therefore, we will need to withdraw from hosting any
  events for attendees throughout the day. Instead, we will focus on maintaining a booth to
  support our community partner.



How likely are you to continue participating in the festival if it was to move to the
downtown Village?

0 Very likely

0 Unlikely

How important is the following for you in terms of your booth or festival activity your
group hosts?

                                          Very Important Important Neutral Not Important
Parking                                          @                0           0                0
Ease of Setup/Cleanup                            @                0           0                0
Friday Setup/Preview                             @                0           0                0
Greenspace (grass)                               @                0           0                0
Hardscape (asphalt/concrete)                     0                0           @                0

Do you have any other suggestions or considerations we should keep in mind/account
for as we evaluate the future location of the festival?

 After ten years of involvement with the Chicken Festival and serving as your community
 partner for several events in the village area, I wanted to share some insights. Over the
 past few years, this festival has grown significantly, surpassing its previous scale in the
 village. While the village has its charm, without the support of local merchants, it risks
 becoming just another street festival.

 Hosting the event at the park allows us to have better control over the area, which is a
 crucial safety consideration in today's climate. Additionally, I believe the overall costs
 would be lower at the park compared to the streets; not to mention that all the
 maintenance equipment and setup supplies are conveniently located nearby. Being able
 to set up partially the evening before offers a significant advantage as well.

 As an event planner, I truly believe that change can revitalize an event. I understand that
 some people may cling to tradition, thinking that "this is how we've always done it."
 However, when the festival moved to the park in 2021, I received feedback like, "Parking
 was terrible here! When is the event moving back to the village?" To those comments, I
 would respond, "Do you understand what you just said?"

 While it's clear that some still prefer the village, the reality is that the festival has outgrown
 that space. Over the past few years, many visitors to our booth-essentially an
 information hub during the event-expressed their enthusiasm for having the festival at
 the park. They've cited the increased space, more shade, additional activities, and the
 great atmosphere created by the music, beer garden, food trucks, and kids' activities. The
 overall sentiment has been overwhelmingly positive.

 If the event were to move back to the village, we might jeopardize newer attractions like
 the cornhole tournament due to space constraints, as well as the beer garden- which
 could create competition with local bars.

 Finally, I want to give a huge shoutout to Sabrina Bernardo and her team for their
 tremendous effort. I know firsthand the hard work that goes into organizing this event, and
 the FORPD is incredibly fortunate to have her leading the way to create such an
 enjoyable experience for our community!



Given the pros and cons of each location, would you prefer the festival to remain at
Fair Oaks Park or return to the downtown Village?

@ Fair Oaks Park
0 downtown Village

 Dear Partner/Vendor,

 Thank you for your participation in the 2024 Fair Oaks Chicken Festival! As you may know,
 the festival was traditionally held in the downtown Village of Fair Oaks but was relocated to
 Fair Oaks Park for the 2021-2024 events due to construction.

 While Fair Oaks Park has offered several advantages and contributed to the festival's
 success in recent years, we are now considering the possibility of returning to the downtown
 Village or permanently keeping the event at Fair Oaks Park.

As a valued partner/vendor, your feedback is important. We would greatly appreciate it if you
could share your thoughts by completing the survey below. Please note that this survey is for
our partner groups/vendors only and only one survey should be completed per partner
group/vendor. Only feedback from an approved 2024 partner/vendor will be reviewed in this
specific survey/feedback form.

Please provide your feedback by November 7, 2024. Please also note that no decisions
have been made-we are currently gathering feedback only. At this stage, we do not have a
definitive date for when the Fair Oaks Recreation & Park District (FORPD) will make the final
decision or who will be involved in that process. We may follow up with partners/vendors
individually for more specific feedback.

Thank you again for your continued support of the Fair Oaks Chicken Festival. We truly value
your input and look forward to hearing your thoughts.



Respondent
You will receive a confirmation by email.

Email

 Dear Partner/Vendor,

Thank you for your participation in the 2024 Fair Oaks Chicken Festival! As you may know,
the festival was traditionally held in the downtown Village of Fair Oaks but was relocated to
Fair Oaks Park for the 2021-2024 events due to construction.

While Fair Oaks Park has offered several advantages and contributed to the festival's
success in recent years, we are now considering the possibility of returning to the downtown
Village or permanently keeping the event at Fair Oaks Park.

As a valued partner/vendor, your feedback is important. We would greatly appreciate it if you
could share your thoughts by completing the survey below. Please note that this survey is for
our partner groups/vendors only and only one survey should be completed per partner
group/vendor. Only feedback from an approved 2024 partner/vendor will be reviewed in this
specific survey/feedback form.

Please provide your feedback by November 7, 2024. Please also note that no decisions
have been made-we are currently gathering feedback only. At this stage, we do not have a
definitive date for when the Fair Oaks Recreation & Park District (FORPD) will make the final
decision or who will be involved in that process. We may follow up with partners/vendors
individually for more specific feedback.

Thank you again for your continued support of the Fair Oaks Chicken Festival. We truly value
your input and look forward to hearing your thoughts.



Respondent
You will receive a confirmation by email.

What are the pros of hosting the festival at Fair Oaks Park?

 Helps bring income to local and independent businesses. Grounds the event in the heart
 of Fair Oaks, making it more intimate, more memorable, and more of a signature event.



What are the cons of hosting the festival at Fair Oaks Park?
  Space may be an issue, but I think it can be done if parking is figured out so roads can be
  used for vendors and open walking space.

What challenges or difficulties did you encounter during the event?

  During vendor load out, we had the vendors wrap around the front parking lot, which was
  GREAT - it went way quicker. The only issue was that there was only one lane in/out of
  the park and as patrons were leaving, vendors were entering, and it was difficult to safely
  meter them.

What went well during the event ? Any standout moments?

  This was by far one of the most enjoyable and smoothest Chicken Festivals I have ever
  worked. I believe that generally, staff were just simply prepared. Despite the fact that we
  didn't have any really bad extraneous incidents (no lost children, no major safety issues/
  injuries, etc.), I still think that even if that did take place that we would have been
  prepared to handle it and that it would not have dampened the positive vibes of the day
  (potentially haha).



What challenges or difficulties did you encounter during the event?

 The only thing I encountered that felt like a challenge was during Vendor Clean Up.
 Snaking vendors in the parking lot so they weren't all in the road on Fair Oaks Blvd. was
 great, but it also blocked people who were parked there and were trying to leave. As
 Alisha was the only person, it was difficult for her to manage as there could have been 2-
 3 people helping to direct traffic. However, we could try to come up with an even better
 system potentially.



Overall, how would you rate the overall origination and execution of the event?




Overall, how would you rate your overall experience working this event?

What improvements, if any, need to be made to safety & security during the event?

  Safety and Security, from my perception, were handled well. Having security, CHP, AND
  Sac Sheriff out at the event is certainly helpful to make people feel more secure, and with
  the event being enclosed and spread out, there's never a time where I feel we have too
  many people in one spot to make it feel unsafe. I felt as though signage was clear and
  visible.



How would you evaluate the marketing for the festival?

                                        Excellent Very good Average Could be improved

Any marketing ideas you would like to share for next year?

 Expand upon our social media presence. We do a decent job at this, but getting the word
 out earlier and more frequently will only benefit us.

 Bring back purchasing of "nicer" posters and flyer EVERYWHERE and anywhere. I know
 we technically already do this, but I think this was a huge influence.

 Expand the FB boosted post marketing budget ever so slightly.

 Collaboration posts featuring the "major" areas of the festival if we have photo/ video too.
 Collaborative posts with Kim, someone from Rotary, etc. where they're talking about the
 festival and shots of the event are playing would be really cool and would increase our
 reach.

 Did you feel the prepaid parking was beneficial?

@ves
ONo


Please provide any changes or suggestions to the pre-paid parking.

  I honestly think that just simply expanding the marketing and outreach will help this be
  successful. I think the limited number of spots could expand from just the lower section to
  the lower and middle section (where we do garage sale) and do well. Now that we've set
  the precedent, I think people will be more apt to want to do it. I did not work physically in
  that area, so I can't say anything on that end.



What changes, if any, would you make to the layout of the event?

 Moving the mainstage was AMAZING!!! It seemed like that was an immensely positive
 change, and it was POPPIN' down there. Also great to have the mainstage be in between
 the alcohol and food.

 I recognize that renting the massive square white teht like we used to was pricey, but I
 wonder if we could re-try the idea of VIP/preferred seating area in the feed court. VIP's
 could get shaded seating at the feed court, a food voucher, a t-shirt, a drink ticket, a
 promo bag of goodies, etc. I know this is something we've already tried, but I think people
 having some sort of wristband so they could come and go to "their spot" would be cool.



How would you evaluate the event vendors?

                                            Excellent Very good Average Could be improved
The layout was                                  @            0           0                0
The variety of vendors                          @            0           0                0
Success of loading and unloading                @            0           0                0

Any suggestions for next year ( vendors / vendor area) ?

 I think the general layout of vendors works for the space that we have. People provide a
 lot of feedback about shade/ clusters/ etc. but for the space we have, I feel as though we
 really maximize it almost as much as possible. Anything more or different would be too
 cluttered and just a mess. People who don't plan the event may not understand that, but
 it's not a simple task to just "put them somewhere else".
  I (Mary), plan to work with Sabrina on moving the kid vendors, not necessarily mixed with
  regular vendors, but elsewhere. I would like to purchase and/or make better signage
  making it clear that these are kid run businesses, and just in general promote that
  marketing aspect a bit more.

Please list pros & cons to keeping CF at Fair Oaks Park.
�---           -- - - --------
                       -      -----
 Cons: Only con I can think of is some issues with accessibility and you don't get the
 "village vibe" ...but...

  Pros:
  •Space andSecurity: This event has felt so much safer and more secure now that it's in a
 space that can be easily fenced in, increased security measures, and the amount of
 space we have is so much more valuable because there are multiple "high points" where
 you can see a vast majority of the event.
  •Set Up andStaffing: Being able to do a big chunk of set up beforehand is HUGE and so
 helpful.There's a lot less staff time required, and it isn't as challenging all in one day as
 opposed to being able to spread it out over a few days.
 • Growth:The event has been able to grow and get better and better each year, and will
 likely only continue to do so.
 • Kid's Park: We've seen a significant decrease in lost children (I think we've had none the
 past two years) with they way the Kid's Parks are set up, and the quality of activities and
 diversity of things to do has increased far more than what we were able to offer in the
 Village.
 • Parking: TONS more parking than the Village. This also enhances safety/ security when
 there isn't as many people parking in front of people's houses.
 • Expansion: There's still more ways to expand the event that we can continue to explore
 and play around with.
 • Event Goer Experience: I've had numerous attendees and participants express how
 much better they think the Park is for this event.



Please list pros & cons to moving CF back to the Village.

 Only pro I can think of is the feel of the event in the Village.

 Cons:
 • With ABC permitting, we would either have to fence the ENTIRE village, or restrict
 people from walking around with alcohol to wherever Rotary is placed which would be
 significantly smaller.
  • We could not do the cornhole tournament.
  • The Kid's Park would shrink in it's capacity to have both areas, amount of activities, and
  way that we offer activities. Way less secure in the Village, we have had next to no lost
  children in FO Park compared to the Village.
  • Vendors would be back to solid pavement which would be extremely hot. There's also
  less space to have as many as we have at FO Park (I think). The Feed Court area has
 shrunk with less space and would be a tricky layout. Potentially would lessen the amount
 of vendors in that area or would have to expand our road closure area.
  • Parking. The event has outgrown the village even moreso than it already had before.
 There simply isn't enough parking / room.
 • Staff Time and Set Up: This event being able to be set up significantly beforehand and
 having access to supplies/yard close by is HUGELY beneficial to the amount of staff time
 and effort put in. We would have to go back to working increased hours across the board,
 and it would be much more challenging to host the event in the Village now.
 • The one benefit to having construction taken so long is that although we have a large
 pool of people who have been to the event in both locations and some of those people
 prefer the Village, we have also had a TON of people who have experienced Chicken
 Festival for the first time in FO Park and also love the location. Change is hard. Altering
 tradition is also very hard. However, sometimes growth and expansion is necessary. This
 decision is necessary.
 • There's probably more I can list, but overall I've heard from NUMEROUS people who've
 attended / been a part of both locations events that say the event HAS to stay, it just
 won't be the same if we move it back.



If CF remains at Fair Oaks Park, what ideas do you have to incorporate the Village?

 • Chicken Cook Off Event?
 • Arts & Entertainment - Some sort of show/musical either themed toward community or
 chickens
 • Similar to Folsom's Sip and Stroll event, Cluck and Crow Stroll or something like that?
 People can shop and do some version of the progressive dinner where they go from
 place to place and stores do special deals?
 • Chicken / Community themed multi-media art gallery and/or contest. Displayed in the
 plaza or at certain businesses and people can either vote or view



Anything else you would like to share about your experience?

 We have an incredible team. I sincerely hope that the decision about this event's location
 will be considered with alllll the feedback in mind, and I hope it's decided to be kept!



What suggestions do you have for making the next event even better?

 I think if we continue to boost the mindset of adding creative ideas, considering the event
 goer's experience and how we can make it better every year, then we're already in good
 shape.

           STAFF REPORT

Meeting Date:       February 19, 2025

To:                 Board of Directors

From:               Michael J. Aho – District Administrator

Subject:            Village Parking Presentation and Update


I.    Recommendation
      This report is for receive and file purposes. Staff request that the Board
      allow Public Comment at tonight's meeting. No additional Staff
      recommendation is planned at this time.

II.   Background
      The renovations at Village Park and its facilities are set to enhance the
      park's appeal and increase visitor numbers to the park and facilities. These
      renovations, funded by Measure J, have been designed to expand and
      enrich the park's facilities and programming. This includes a variety of new
      community events, theatrical performances, and educational programs.
      However, even before the reopening of the renovated facilities, parking
      within the Village is already at a premium, struggling to meet current
      demands. This situation underscores a critical issue: the existing parking
      infrastructure is insufficient to accommodate the daily influx of visitors,
      program participants, and local business customers.

      The key groups affected by this limitation include:
      Drop-In Park Users: Casual visitors, including individuals and families,
      who come to enjoy the park's recreational amenities.
      Program and Event Attendees: People attending scheduled events such
      as concerts, theater shows, and classes.
      Facility Renters: Guests at private events held in the Community
      Clubhouse, Black Box Theatre, Community Rooms and Veteran’s Memorial
      Amphitheater.
      Local Business Customers: Patrons of the Village's businesses.
       As we approach the grand reopening of Village Park, the pre-existing
       parking shortfall is expected to become more pronounced. Parking
       management is not just about enhancing park accessibility but is crucial for
       addressing the ongoing and increasing strain on parking resources.

       Staff conducted Public Outreach meetings on February 8 and February 12
       to engage with the community regarding the management of parking
       around Village Park. Approximately 30 people attended each session. These
       meetings were designed to inform and gather comments from the
       community about potential changes to parking management. See summary
       and recording of those meetings on Attachment B.

       Before initiating our public outreach, Board Chair Tamagni and I met with
       county staff, including Supervisor Desmond of District 3, to outline our plans
       and discuss the potential for managing parking around Plaza Park, ensuring
       they were fully informed of our efforts.

III.   Problem /Situation/ Request
       District staff is exploring the potential for managing parking to enhance
       accessibility for park users and support local businesses effectively.
       Currently, there are no parking restrictions, which leads to over-extended
       parking durations that can disadvantage park users, visitors and customers
       of local businesses.

       We are investigating several legal considerations with our District Attorney
       and Bond Counsel to ensure any changes align with FORPD’s operational
       scope as defined by Public Resources Code, Section 5780. At this juncture,
       staff are not making a recommendation until further legal advice is
       obtained. To keep the Board informed and involved, staff will provide
       further updates on this project at a future Board meeting, potentially in
       March or April.


IV.    Financial Analysis
       District Attorney fees which are not known at this time.

Respectfully Submitted,


Michael J. Aho
District Administrator

Introduction
   + Background

Background
Overview of Special District Limitations:
•   Special districts like FORPD are established to serve specific functions
    within a defined area and have distinct legal and operational boundaries.
1. Limited Scope of Services:
•   We can only offer services that are authorized by enabling legislation,
    specifically Public Resources Code, Section 5780.
•   Services are limited to parks and recreation; FORPD cannot provide police,
    fire, public works, housing, or economic development services.
2. No Authority Over Land Use & Zoning:
•   All zoning, permitting, and land-use decisions are under the jurisdiction of
    Sacramento County.
•   FORPD lacks the authority to approve or deny development projects or
    enforce zoning regulations.
3. Funding Restrictions:
•   FORPD’s financial resources are strictly allocated to parks and recreation
    services.
•   Funds, such as those from Measure J bonds, are dedicated and cannot be
    used for purposes outside of the district’s scope.


4. No General Government Powers:
•   Unlike city or county governments, FORPD does not possess broad
    governmental powers and must operate within its defined mandate.
•   Essential services such as public safety, street maintenance, and utilities to
    name a few are provided by the county or other designated entities, not
    FORPD.
5. Legal Compliance & Accountability:
•   We must follow state laws and county regulations which direct what we can
    and cannot do.
•   Any attempt to expand services beyond the authorized scope requires
    formal approval through legislative changes and unauthorized expansion
    could result in legal and financial consequences.
Conclusion:
•   We are committed to enhancing community parks and recreational
    opportunities but must navigate within our legal and financial constraints.
•   Understanding these limitations is essential for maintaining compliance,
    financial integrity, and focused delivery on our mission to serve the
    community effectively.

Establishment Date: October 8, 1945

authority for a class of special districts that provides community recreation, park,
and open-space facilities and recreation services within specified boundaries and
under local control.”

       general obligation bonds could only be used to finance acquisition and
                  improvement of real property for District purposes.”

Management
                                     Managed Parking

Purpose: Enhance accessibility for park users, visitors, and support local businesses.

Measure J Alignment: Ensures parking space improvements funded by Measure J primarily
benefit park visitors, aligning with the bond's intent for real property improvement.
                              Benefits of Managed Parking:
• Increased Turnover: Managed Parking can increase the turnover of parking spaces,
allowing more people to access Park, programs and businesses, throughout the day.


• Reduced Congestion: By encouraging drivers to vacate spaces managed parking can
  help reduce the congestion caused by drivers circling the area looking for parking.


• Fair Access: Can provide more drivers with a fair chance to find parking near their
  destination, rather than allowing a few vehicles to occupy spaces for extended periods.


• Boost to Local Economy: Turnover can increase the number of visitors to an area,
  potentially boosting sales for local shops, cafes, and services as more customers can
  stop by.
                                                             • Multiple Payment Options: A variety of
                                                               payment options, including most major
                                                               credit cards, Google Pay, Apple Pay, and
                                                               PayPal.
                                                             • Phone Number: To make parking
                                                               payments for people without a
                                                               smartphone
                                                             • Pay in Person: The District Office can
                                                               receive payment in person Mon-Fri 9am-
                                                               5pm.
                                                             • Drop Box: At District Office after 5pm or
                                                               weekends.




● Notifications: Text and email alerts to notify a user when parking will expire.
● Extend Time: Ability to add time to existing parking session to avoid running back to “feed the
  meter.”

     attendees and facility rentals

    the event and would expire
    when the event is over.

  • Code would only work if a
    parking spot is available. No
    Guarantee of spots

           STAFF REPORT

Meeting Date:            February 19, 2025
To:                      Board of Directors
From:                    Michael J. Aho – District Administrator
Subject:                 FY 2022/2023 Financial Audit
Prepared By:             Jennifer Larkin – Administrative Services Manger

 I.    Recommendation
       Approve the Annual Financial Audit for FY 2022/2023.
II.    Background
       Richardson & Company, LLP performed the FY 2022/2023 audit; a copy of
       which is attached (Attachment B). A presentation on the audit findings and
       general financial health of the District by Ingrid Sheipline from Richardson &
       Company, LLP will be made at the regular February Board meeting.
III.   Problem /Situation/ Request
       The 2022/2023 Audit did not identify any deficiencies in internal controls that
       might be material weaknesses. District staff and the District’s contracted CPA
       reviewed the Draft Audit. The audit did identify some financial and procedural
       practices that the District should consider amending which are listed in the
       Governance Letter (Attachment C). The Governance Letter also outlines the
       audit process and enumerates any adjustments the auditors made during the
       audit.
IV.    Financial Analysis
       The District’s final budget for fiscal year 2023/2024 included funding for
       independent audit services.
Respectfully Submitted,


Michael J. Aho
District Administrator

                                  INDEPENDENT AUDITOR’S REPORT


Board of Directors
Fair Oaks Recreation and Park District
Fair Oaks, California


Opinions

We have audited the accompanying financial statements of the governmental activities, each major fund,
and the aggregate remaining fund information of the Fair Oaks Recreation and Park District (the District)
as of and for the year ended June 30, 2023, and the related notes to the financial statements, which
collectively comprise the District’s basic financial statements as listed in the table of contents.

In our opinion, the financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the
respective financial position of the governmental activities, each major fund, and the aggregate remaining
fund information of the District as of June 30, 2023, and the respective changes in financial position for
the year then ended in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of
America.

Basis for Opinions

We conducted our audit in accordance with auditing standards generally accepted in the United States of
America.      Our responsibilities under those standards are further described in the Auditor’s
Responsibilities for the Audit of the Financial Statements section of our report. We are required to be
independent of the District and to meet our other ethical responsibilities, in accordance with the relevant
ethical requirements relating to our audit. We believe that the audit evidence we have obtained is
sufficient and appropriate to provide a basis for our audit opinions.

Responsibilities of Management for the Financial Statements

Management is responsible for the preparation and fair presentation of these financial statements in
accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America; this includes
the design, implementation, and maintenance of internal control relevant to the preparation and fair
presentation of financial statements that are free from material misstatement, whether due to fraud or
error.

In preparing the financial statements, management is required to evaluate whether there are conditions or
events, considered in the aggregate, that raise substantial doubt about the District’s ability to continue as a
going concern for twelve months beyond the financial statement date, including any currently known
information that may raise substantial doubt shortly thereafter.




                                                      1
Board of Directors
Fair Oaks Recreation and Park District

Auditor’s Responsibilities for the Audit of the Financial Statements

Our objectives are to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements as a whole are
free from material misstatement, whether due to fraud or error, and to issue an auditor’s report that
includes our opinions. Reasonable assurance is a high level of assurance but is not absolute assurance and
therefore is not a guarantee that an audit conducted in accordance with generally accepted auditing
standards will always detect a material misstatement when it exists. The risk of not detecting a material
misstatement resulting from fraud is higher than for one resulting from error, as fraud may involve
collusion, forgery, intentional omissions, misrepresentations, or the override of internal control.
Misstatements are considered material if there is a substantial likelihood that, individually or in the
aggregate, they would influence the judgment made by a reasonable user based on the financial
statements.

In performing an audit in accordance with generally accepted auditing standards, we:

       Exercise professional judgment and maintain professional scepticism throughout the audit.

       Identify and assess the risks of material misstatement of the financial statements, whether due to
        fraud or error, and design and perform audit procedures responsive to those risks. Such
        procedures include examining, on a test basis, evidence regarding the amounts and disclosures in
        the financial statements.

       Obtain an understanding of internal control relevant to the audit in order to design audit
        procedures that are appropriate in the circumstances, but not for the purpose of expressing an
        opinion on the effectiveness of the District’s internal control. Accordingly, no such opinion is
        expressed.

       Evaluate the appropriateness of accounting policies used and the reasonableness of significant
        accounting estimates made by management, as well as evaluate the overall presentation of the
        financial statements.

       Conclude whether, in our judgment, there are conditions or events, considered in the aggregate,
        that raise substantial doubt about the District’s ability to continue as a going concern for a
        reasonable period of time.

We are required to communicate with those charged with governance regarding, among other matters, the
planned scope and timing of the audit, significant audit findings, and certain internal control-related
matters that we identified during the audit.

Required Supplementary Information

Accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America require that the management’s
discussion, analysis and budgetary comparison information, schedule of changes in the net pension
liability and related ratios, schedule of contributions to the pension plan, and schedule of changes in the
net OPEB liability and related ratios and schedule of contributions to the OPEB Plan be presented to
supplement the basic financial statements. Such information is the responsibility of management and,
although not a part of the basic financial statements, is required by the Governmental Accounting
Standards Board, who considers it to be an essential part of financial reporting for placing the basic
financial statements in an appropriate operational, economic, or historical context. We have applied
certain limited procedures to the required supplementary information in accordance with auditing
standards generally accepted in the United States of America, which consisted of inquiries of
management about the methods of preparing the information and comparing the information for
consistency with management’s responses to our inquiries, the basic financial statements, and other

Board of Directors

knowledge we obtained during our audit of the basic financial statements. We do not express an opinion
or provide any assurance on the information because the limited procedures do not provide us with
sufficient evidence to express an opinion or provide any assurance.
